<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Terrorism in Europe</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Ireland&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrorism in Ireland">Terrorism in Ireland</a>)</span></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:637px;max-width:637px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Atocha_Station_makeshift_shrine_march_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="2004 height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Atocha_Station_makeshift_shrine_march_2004.jpg/360px-Atocha_Station_makeshift_shrine_march_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/Atocha_Station_makeshift_shrine_march_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_India_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Air India Flight 182 bombing" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Air_India_Memorial.jpg/120px-Air_India_Memorial.jpg" width="120" height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Air_India_Memorial.jpg/180px-Air_India_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Air_India_Memorial.jpg/240px-Air_India_Memorial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:267px;max-width:267px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg" class="image"><img alt="City of Poros cruise ship attack" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg/265px-%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg" width="265" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg/398px-%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg/530px-%22City_of_Poros%22_-_1988.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1199" data-file-height="812" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The <a href="/wiki/2004_Madrid_train_bombings" title="2004 Madrid train bombings">bombings of the Madrid train system in 2004</a> (left, makeshift shrine), the <a href="/wiki/Air_India_Flight_182" title="Air India Flight 182">bombing of Air India Flight 182</a> in 1985 (centre, memorial), and the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Poros_ship_attack" title="City of Poros ship attack"><i>City of Poros</i> ship attack</a> in 1988 (right, <i>City of Poros</i> in 1988) constitute the deadliest attacks carried out in Europe on land, in aviation, and in nautical transport respectively, killing 192, 329, and 11 people.</div></div></div>
<p>There is a long history of <b>terrorism in Europe</b>. This has often been linked to nationalist and separatist movements, while other acts have been related to political extremism (including anarchism, far-right and far-left extremism), or religious extremism.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is an overlap between terrorism and various other forms of conflict and violent action, including <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">civil wars</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> or non-international armed conflicts. This is the case with several significant non-international conflicts in Europe, where there thus can be dispute as to what counts as terrorism: examples include the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">Irish War of Independence</a> (1919–21), the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a> and subsequent conflicts,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/First_Chechen_War" title="First Chechen War">First</a> (1994–6) and <a href="/wiki/Second_Chechen_War" title="Second Chechen War">Second Chechen Wars</a> (1999–2009), and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Dagestan" title="War of Dagestan">War of Dagestan</a> (1999).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the Middle Ages, maritime nations in Europe sponsored <a href="/wiki/Piracy#Europe_and_North_Africa" title="Piracy">pirates</a> and privateering against rivals.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The term "terror" is used about the <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_terror" class="mw-redirect" title="Reign of terror">reign of terror</a> in France, carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Jacobins" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacobins">Jacobins</a>, 1792-4.
</p>

</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#ddf; text-align:center;">Response to terrorism</div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">Counter-terrorism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_conventions_on_terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="International conventions on terrorism">International conventions</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anti-terrorism_legislation" title="Anti-terrorism legislation">Anti-terrorism legislation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Terrorism_insurance" title="Terrorism insurance">Terrorism insurance</a></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;padding-top:0.25em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Terrorism" title="Template:Terrorism"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Terrorism" title="Template talk:Terrorism"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Terrorism&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Terrorism in Europe around the beginning of the twentieth century was often associated with <a href="/wiki/Anarchist_terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anarchist terrorism">anarchism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Terrorism within the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> since 1951 has often been linked to separatist movements, including the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army" title="Irish Republican Army">Irish Republican Army</a> within the United Kingdom, and <a href="/wiki/Euskadi_Ta_Askatasuna" class="mw-redirect" title="Euskadi Ta Askatasuna">Euskadi Ta Askatasuna</a> within Spain. Other perpetrators have been linked to far-right and far-left extremism, environmental extremism and anarchism. Since 2001, there has been an increase in attacks linked to extremist Islamist groups, particularly in France. Many separatist terrorist activities also have a religious angle, as, for example, with Chechen separatism in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. The internationally co-ordinated element has seen increasing attempts by governments to seek to weaken extremist ideology, particularly <a href="/wiki/Islamic_extremism" title="Islamic extremism">Islamic extremism</a>.
</p><p>It remains the case that the majority of deaths from terrorism do not occur in the "<a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">West</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> When the Al Qaeda attacks against the United States in 2001 are excluded, only 0.5% of all deaths from terrorism have occurred in Western countries &#8211; European nations, United States, Canada and Australia &#8211; in the years 2000-14.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Terrorism_Index_page_2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Terrorism_Index_page_2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> However, there have been recent increases in the number of high-fatality attacks. There had been a decrease in the number of overall fatalities from terrorist attacks between 1990 and 2015, compared to those between 1970 and 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Economic_Forum_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Economic_Forum-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Prior to 1990, on average 150 people died each year from terrorist attacks; this figure would be even higher if the large number of people who died in 1988 from the Pan Am 2013 bombing were included. From 1990, an average of a little under 50 people died each year. However, this figure has begun to increase again from 2011, with the attacks by far-right extremist Anders Breivik in Norway, and Islamist extremist attacks in France in 2015 and 2016.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a> has published an annual trend report on terrorist attacks (including failed, foiled, and completed attacks) and terrorist related arrests in the EU since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Europol_statistics_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europol_statistics-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The reports identify that perpetrators' known or suspected affiliations have been disparate in nature. Europol break these down into five categories: <a href="/wiki/Jihadist_terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="Jihadist terrorism">jihadist terrorism</a> (previously termed "religiously-inspired terrorism"); <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_terrorism" title="Nationalist terrorism">ethno-nationalist and separatist terrorism</a>; <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_terrorism" title="Left-wing terrorism">left-wing and anarchist terrorism</a>; <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_terrorism" title="Right-wing terrorism">right-wing terrorism</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Special-interest_terrorism" title="Special-interest terrorism">single-issue terrorism</a>. Europol's reports do not provide a breakdown of the proportion of attacks that have been completed or the type of damage inflicted. According to these data the vast majority of terrorist attacks in the EU between 2006 and 2013 are affiliated with ethno-national or separatist motives, followed by left-wing attacks and those that are registered as 'unspecified'. A significant number of terror attacks are motivated religiously or associated with right-wing groups. However, among those arrested on terror-related crimes most are religiously motivated and form the largest group, followed by separatist related terror suspects.
</p><p>In 2015, a total of 211 completed, failed, or foiled terrorist attacks were reported by EU states, resulting in 151 fatalities (of which 148 were in France, with 130 of them occurring during the <a href="/wiki/November_2015_Paris_attacks" title="November 2015 Paris attacks">November 2015 Paris attacks</a>) and over 360 people injured. As in previous years, separatist attacks accounted for the largest proportion (65), followed by jihadist attacks (17). The latter, however, caused the largest number of fatalities (150) and injuries (250). The United Kingdom reported the largest number of attacks (103), but did not provide statistics on suspected affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-Europol_statistics2015_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europol_statistics2015-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
Tackling jihadist terrorism threats has become an over-riding priority for security services, although many commentators express concerns that the risk of far-right terrorism is currently being underestimated.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_29_Feb_2016_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_29_Feb_2016-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, British intelligence <a href="/wiki/MI5" title="MI5">MI5</a> said that <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> is the most concentrated area of terrorist activity "probably anywhere in Europe", with weekly threats from dissident Irish republicans.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention">Prevention</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Prevention">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_twentieth_century">Early twentieth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early twentieth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>European states were at the fore of plans for an international criminal court under the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> in the 1930s, working through the Committee for the Repression of Terrorism (CRT). The CRT sought to define terrorism and get nation's domestic policies to support anti-terrorism activities. Opposition by Britain and tensions over fascism in Germany and Italy limited the final proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europol">Europol</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Europol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europol_Building;_The_Hague;_Eisenhowerlaan;_Statenkwartier;_2014;_photo_nr._41860.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Europol_Building%3B_The_Hague%3B_Eisenhowerlaan%3B_Statenkwartier%3B_2014%3B_photo_nr._41860.jpg/220px-Europol_Building%3B_The_Hague%3B_Eisenhowerlaan%3B_Statenkwartier%3B_2014%3B_photo_nr._41860.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Europol_Building%3B_The_Hague%3B_Eisenhowerlaan%3B_Statenkwartier%3B_2014%3B_photo_nr._41860.jpg/330px-Europol_Building%3B_The_Hague%3B_Eisenhowerlaan%3B_Statenkwartier%3B_2014%3B_photo_nr._41860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Europol_Building%3B_The_Hague%3B_Eisenhowerlaan%3B_Statenkwartier%3B_2014%3B_photo_nr._41860.jpg/440px-Europol_Building%3B_The_Hague%3B_Eisenhowerlaan%3B_Statenkwartier%3B_2014%3B_photo_nr._41860.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europol_Building;_The_Hague;_Eisenhowerlaan;_Statenkwartier;_2014;_photo_nr._41860.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The seat of the <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">European Police Office</a> (Europol) in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>European cooperation in the field of counter-terrorism include the <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">European Police Office</a> (Europol), an EU <a href="/wiki/Agency_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Agency of the European Union">agency</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a>. <a href="/wiki/TREVI" title="TREVI">TREVI</a> was an early example of EU cooperation in this field.
</p><p>The main transnational activity to combat terrorism in recent years has been through Europol. They have categorised acts of terrorism that have either failed, been foiled or been successfully executed within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) as either pertaining to religious issues, right wing, left wing or separatist movements. The field is subject to considerable cooperation among national authorities.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual_countries">Individual countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Individual countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2014 the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_France" title="Government of France">Government of France</a> introduced legislation to combat terrorism by toughening surveillance, making it lawful to detain individuals linked to radical "Islamist" groups, and to block Internet sites that incite anti-Semitism, terrorism and hatred. The country's Interior Minister Bernard Cazeneuve revealed 600 French nationals were in Syria at the time or planned to go there. The bill includes a ban on foreign travel for up to six months for those believed to hold terrorist sympathies, provides for the confiscation and invalidation of passports,  and prohibits airlines from allowing such individuals to fly.<sup id="cite_ref-FranceTerrorism_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FranceTerrorism-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 2005, the United Kingdom government introduced the CONTEST strategy, which seeks to improve co-operation between security services, and other public and private organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-CONTEST:_The_United_Kingdom&#39;s_Strategy_for_Countering_Terrorism_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONTEST:_The_United_Kingdom&#39;s_Strategy_for_Countering_Terrorism-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> This includes four strands, namely Pursue, (seeking to apprehend potential terrorists), Prevent, (seeking to reduce risks of 'radicalisation', deter potential terrorists and share information), Protect, (seeking to ensure the security of potential targets and organisations is optimised), and Prepare, (seeking to ensure an effective response in the immediate aftermath of any attack).  Similar strategies have been adopted by other countries across the European Union, and there have been increases in co-operation between nations and security forces.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deadliest_attacks">Deadliest attacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrorism_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Deadliest attacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is a list of terrorist incidents in Europe which resulted in at least ten deaths. It lists attacks on civilians by <a href="/wiki/Violent_non-state_actor" title="Violent non-state actor">non-state actors</a> that are widely referred to as terrorism. It excludes transcontinental countries such as Turkey and Russia, which have most of their landmass in another continent. For incidents in Russia, see <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Russia" title="Terrorism in Russia">Terrorism in Russia</a> and for incidents in Istanbul, see <a href="/wiki/Terror_attacks_in_Istanbul_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Terror attacks in Istanbul (disambiguation)">Terror attacks in Istanbul</a>.
</p>
<dl><dt>Key: motivation</dt></dl>
